Le somnambulisme peut être considéré quelquefois comme une existence inférieure à celle de la veille, aussi nous pré- sente-t-il des faits de ce genre : « Un individu, somnambule naturel, est frappé du nombre de vers en iqtie qu’il vient de lire, il s’en moque; le soir, il s’endort en n’y pensant plus. Le lendemain, il trouve son carnet sur lequel il a écrit pendant la nuit 75 vers en ique sur le même sujet ^ : Oh ! toi qui sais chanter sur ton luth poétique La gloire du prélat et la vertu civique, Permets, fils d’Apollon, que ma muse pudique Se revête pour toi de sa blanche tunique… etc. Une autre malade hystéro-épileptique imite dans son som- meil naturel tous les bruits qu’elle a entendus dans la journée. Just as the unleashing of passions is complete in a dream ^ just as a long-dormant inclination during waking takes over the empire it once had during a dream ^ so weak impulses in a state can become all-powerful in another. Three hysterics were in the same ward of the hospital and, as often happens, hardly loved each other and affected in quite different ways, during their normal state;

    but, when they were in crisis, they copied each other so well that they had the same delirium and pronounced exactly the same words. Now, for at least one that I had seen in another room, this form of crisis and this kind of delirium that she did not have before was a ‘Moreau (from Tours). Hashish, 137. * Id. Morbid Psychology, 404. ‘The Revealer of Magnetism ^ April, 1838. ^ Journal of Magnetism, 1855, 487. s Maury. Sleep, 87. ° Charma. Some sleep. 1852, 19. pure imitation. The hashish gives a disposition of this kind: “it produces in the will, in the instincts, such a relaxation that we become the plaything of the most diverse impressions. By a word, by a gesture, our thoughts can be turned on a host of subjects ^ ”The intoxication of hashish resembles, moreover, says M. Richet ^, in the hysterical state and one finds there the same exaggeration of feeling. and the same helplessness of the will. All ideas are translated without our being able to prevent them. As in catalepsy, the automatism of ideas is sometimes revealed, not only by their duration,

    but also by their associations; we see certain acts thus explained by involuntary connections between ideas. “We know the story of this poor young man from the house of Mailly, of whom La Palatine speaks in her memoirs. A sachet had been given to him by M “^ de la Forge; bewitched by the magical power of this sachet, he begged his family to consent to the marriage. The refusals despaired him and he resolved to drown,

    but hardly had he removed the bag that charm ceased and the most icy indifference succeeded passion. ”How many stupidities, crimes committed under the influence of a spell, as the consequence of a fixed idea, could be explained in the same way. One has lost, as in the dream, the power to direct the thoughts; they develop in their own way, and one or the other, last if not all, arrives at full execution. In this case the action seems even more irresistible, for it does not run up against the other ideas of consciousness, it comes out of them quite naturally; just as we are not astonished at our own dreams, so hysterics and sleepwalkers are seldom surprised at their own absurdities, for they do not have opposing images in their minds which can serve as a point of comparison. . This association of ideas still has, especially in these people, a singular effect which it is necessary to know well; it is often exercised by contrast, and the thought of a thing rapidly brings into it the idea, then the execution of the absolutely opposite thing; “They ‘Moreau (from Tours). Haschich, 66. * Ch. Richet. Man and intelligence, 124. ^ De Gasparin. The rotating tables, 1855,1, 427. want to laugh when they see people cry, say inappropriate words when they think of being modest, and so on. ^ “. This association by contrast which we have already pointed out exists in a natural way before it presents itself in the experiences of the transference. In short, there is not a single character of the suggested acts which does not find its analogue in the natural conduct of these constantly suggestible individuals. Let us now make the same study of the feelings and passions of these same weak personalities, still in the same states as we have described, when, either through illness or through hypnotizing processes, the field of their consciousness has been restricted and not can contain more simultaneously than a number of images much less than that which it should regularly contain. It is commonplace observation that people of this kind are extraordinarily emotional and that, for the slightest pretext, they seem to experience with unheard-of violence all the jolts of joy, sorrow, love, death. - reur, etc. Examples abound. It was enough to tell in front of Lucie (awake or at first somnambulism) some absurd story of a crushed dog or of a husband who beats his wife, for her to immediately change her face and withdraw into a corner, weeping like a Magdalene. . The joy of seeing me again overwhelms Léonie, and for a few minutes there are shocks, sobs, inarticulate cries, almost the beginning of a nervous breakdown. It is in this way, moreover, by a veritable nervous breakdown that all of Rose’s emotions end; I saw it, for forty-eight hours, in a series of almost continual fits of disappointment, because someone she was expecting had not come to see her. What should we think of this suddenness and this violence in emotion? Let us first notice that the expression of emotion is here, if I am not mistaken, much more violent than the emotion itself. These great upheavals of their whole being, when they have not yet brought about the crisis, because then the nature of the phenomena changes, calms down as quickly as they were provoked. We must not try to console a hysteric, * Liébault. Sleep, 235. as one would do for an ordinary person, by talking to him about the object of his grief and showing him that it is futile. No, if we are talking about object that caused their anger or their despair,

    however we talk about it, we increase their cries and tears. It is quite simply necessary, without any art of transitions, to speak abruptly of something completely different: they remain for a moment taken aback, hesitating; then, in a few seconds, give themselves completely to the new subject and laugh merrily when they still have tears in their eyes. Leonie had lost a child a few years ago under the saddest circumstances, and for the poor woman it was a very just cause of sorrow. The most trivial incidents, a consonance, a date, the black color of a piece of paper, reminded her every moment of the misfortune when she was sleepwalking, and did not remind her of it when she was awake. It was tears and cries then, then interminable contracts. At first I tried to console her,

    but in vain; It was not until quite late that I thought of the real way to stop this grief. As soon as her face grew sad and she started to cry: “Oh! my poor little one, ”I suddenly spoke to her about something else, she started laughing and it was over. Much better, if we succeed in making them confess what they are feeling, we see that in reality they feel very little. One day, Lucie, who was in total anesthetic and did not even feel a strong burn, cut her hand and the blood flowed rather heavily. She began to cry and cry as if she was going through real martyrdom. I was a little surprised because, at that very moment, she did not feel a pin stuck in her hand without warning her, and I asked her if she was in a lot of pain: “

    but… no, not precisely,” she said, “but you see, my blood is flowing. I must suffer a lot, it is only natural that I cry out… ah!… ”I found this word which escaped him very significant; she does not cry because she is really in pain, here I think she felt nothing,

    but because she must be in pain. A more or less vague idea of ​​suffering, perhaps with a very faint hallucinatory image of old pain, that was all there was below those loud cries and despair. In some cases, it will be said, the emotion is very real; Léonie’s grief when thinking of her child, is terrified of Lucie during her crisis, are true feelings. That is fine,

    but that does not prevent the expression of emotion from still playing a large role; for I am disposed to believe here that the real feeling is posterior to the external expression. A well-known American psychologist, Mr. William James, has supported a very attractive theory about the origin of emotions *. According to him, it is wrong to say with common sense: We are losing our fortune, we are sorrowful, we cry. “This order is not correct, the second mental state is not immediately introduced by the first, the physical manifestations must be interposed between them. The rational order is that we feel sorrow because we cry, anger because we hit, etc. All our thoughts produce in us physical modifications, movements, modifications of circulation, of respiration, of the condition of the skin, glands, bladder, etc. By a kind of feedback shock, the sensitivity brings back to consciousness the notion of these changes and gives us an emotion which is precisely only the more or less confused sensation of all these modifications. The author concluded that a totally insensitive individual should not be aware of these organic changes and therefore no longer experience emotions, and he wrote to me about this when, in my early studies, I had reported Lucie as a total anesthetic. I told him that hysterics seemed pretty bad to me the condition of the skin, glands, bladder, etc. By a kind of feedback shock, the sensitivity brings back to consciousness the notion of these changes and gives us an emotion which is precisely only the more or less confused sensation of all these modifications.
